Conditions for Valid Hearing (Samaʿ) in Hadith Transmission
Explaining the conditions of attentiveness during hadith hearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions required for a valid auditory reception of hadith and state the exception for necessity.

Core Idea
Attentiveness is key for valid hadith hearing; distraction invalidates transmission except in necessity.

In usul al-fiqh, the reliability of hadith transmission depends on the method of acquisition. Al-Bazdawi rules that for hearing (samaʿ) to be a valid proof, the listener must be fully attentive. Distractions such as looking at another book, writing, playing, or sleeping render the transmission unacceptable, unless the situation is one of necessity where the person is excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is auditory reception (samaʿ) of hadith. Its validity requires the listener to be attentive and not distracted.
Attentiveness is the core condition.
2
List the prohibited distractions
The passage mentions looking at another book, writing, turning away with amusement, heedlessness due to sleep or laziness.
These all indicate lack of focus.
3
Understand the exception
If a distraction occurs out of necessity (darurah), the person is excused and his transmission is still accepted.
Necessity makes the invalid valid.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario, decide whether the hearing is valid based on attentiveness.
Use the list of distractions.
5
Note the implication for proof
If hearing is invalid, the transmitted hadith does not establish proof (hujja) and the chain is broken.
This rule ensures reliability.

أما الأول : فالحفظ من غير واسطة الخط، وهذا فضل خُص به رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام؛ لقوة نور القلب، استغنى عن الخط، وكانوا لا يكتبون) من قبل، ثم صارت الكتابةُ سُنَّةٌ في الكتاب والحديث؛ صيانةً
(۱) قوله : وكانوا لا يكتبون ليس كلهم، بل بعضهم.
فممن كره ذلك: علي رضي الله عنه : روى عنه ابن أبي شيبة: «أعزِم على كل من فمَحَاه، فإنما هلك الناس حيث تتبعوا أحاديث علمائهم، وتركوا عنده كتاب إلا رجع کتاب ربهم.
وأبو سعيد الخدري قد روى عنه ابن أبي شيبة : خذوا عنا كما أخذنا عن نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم.
وابن مسعود : وأخرج عنه أنه كان يكره كتاب العلم.
وروي عن الشعبي: «أن مروان دعا زيد بن ثابت وقوماً يكتبون وهو لا يدري، فأعلموه ، فقال : لعل كل حديث حدثتكم ليس كما حدثتكم».
وعن سعيد بن جبير قال: كنا نختلف في أشياء، فكتبتها في كتاب، ثم أتيتُ بها ابن عمر أسأله عنها خفياً، فلو علم بها كانت الفيصل فيما بيني وبينه».
And as for one who sits in a gathering of hearing while he is occupied with looking at a book other than what is being read, or writes with a pen, or turns away from it with amusement or play, or is heedless due to sleep or laziness, then he has no precision and no trustworthiness, and it is feared that he will be deprived of his share, and Allah forbid, so proof is not established by someone like him, nor is the chain of transmission connected through his report, except what occurs out of necessity: then it is excused and its person is excused. And if hearing is valid, memorization becomes obligatory until the time of performance. That is also of two types: complete and what is less than that at the time of comparison. The first: absolute determination (ʿazīmah), and the second: a concession (rukhaṣah) that has turned into determination. As for the first: it is memorization without the medium of writing; this is a virtue that was specifically granted to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) because of the strength of the light of the heart, he was independent of writing. And they used not to write before, then writing became a sunnah (established practice) in the Book and the hadith for preservation. (1) His statement: 'and they used not to write' is not all of them, but some of them. Among those who disliked that: ʿAlī (may Allah be pleased with him): Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from him: 'I adjure everyone who has a book except that he returns [and erases it]? For the people perished only when they followed the hadiths of their scholars and left the Book of their Lord.' And Abu Saʿīd al-Khudrī: Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from him: 'Take from us as we took from our Prophet (peace be upon him).' And Ibn Masʿūd: it is reported from him that he disliked writing of knowledge. And from al-Shaʿbī: 'Marwan called Zayd ibn Thābit and some people to write while he did not know, so they informed him, and he said: "Perhaps every hadith I narrated to you is not as I narrated it."' And from Saʿīd ibn Jubayr: 'We used to differ on matters, and I wrote them in a book, then I brought it to Ibn ʿUmar to ask him secretly. If he had known, it would have been the decisive factor between me and him.'
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions for a valid hearing (samaʿ) in hadith transmission. The author begins by stating that a person who is distracted during a hadith session—whether by looking at another book, writing, playing, or sleeping—lacks the precision and trustworthiness required for reliable transmission. Such a person's report does not establish proof, nor is his chain accepted, except in cases of necessity where he is excused. This emphasizes the importance of attentiveness in the learning process.

Then the author discusses the obligation of memorization after valid hearing. Memorization is obligatory until the time of performance. He distinguishes two types: complete memorization without the aid of writing, which is an absolute determination (ʿazīmah) and was a special virtue of the Prophet ﷺ, and lesser memorization that is aided by writing, which originally was a concession (rukhaṣah) but later turned into a firm practice. The author notes that writing became a sunnah for the preservation of the Quran and hadith.

He then provides a historical footnote: the statement 'they used not to write' applies only to some, not all. He lists several companions who disliked writing hadith, including ʿAlī, Abu Saʿīd al-Khudrī, and Ibn Masʿūd, and reports from al-Shaʿbī and Saʿīd ibn Jubayr that show caution about writing. This demonstrates the early diversity of opinion on the permissibility of writing hadith, though eventually writing became the norm for preservation.

Key Terms
سماع (samāʿ): Auditory reception of hadith in a formal gathering.
حفظ (ḥifẓ): Memorization of the transmitted content.
عزيمة (ʿazīmah): An original or strict obligation without concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a person's hearing to be a valid proof in hadith transmission?
A) He must write down what he hears
B) He must be attentive and not distracted
C) He must have memorized all hadith perfectly
D) He must be a companion of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Valid hearing requires attentiveness; distractions invalidate transmission except in necessity.

Obligation of Memorization and the Role of Writing in Hadith Preservation
Explaining the obligation of memorization and the historical debate on writing hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two types of memorization after valid hearing and state the Hanafi view that writing is a sunnah for preservation.

Core Idea
After valid hearing, memorization is obligatory; it can be complete (without writing) or aided by writing, which changed from a concession to a firm practice.

Once a hadith is heard validly, the transmitter must ensure its preservation until he narrates it. Al-Bazdawi distinguishes between two levels: complete memorization (ideal) and memorization aided by writing (originally a concession that became a sunnah). The passage also presents historical evidence that some early companions disliked writing hadith, but later scholars adopted it for preservation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
After valid hearing, memorization becomes wajib (obligatory) until the time of performance.
This ensures accuracy in transmission.
2
Distinguish the two types
Type 1: Complete memorization without the medium of writing (azimah). Type 2: Memorization with the aid of writing (originally rukhsah, then turned into azimah).
The first was the Prophet's ﷺ practice.
3
Understand the change in status of writing
Writing was initially a concession (rukhsah) because of the strength of memory, but later became a sunnah (established practice) for preservation.
Necessity turned concession into firm obligation.
4
Explore the historical context
Early companions like Ali, Abu Saeed, and Ibn Masud disliked writing for fear of mixing with Quran, but eventually writing became standard.
The passage includes quotes showing this diversity.
5
Apply the rule
In evaluating a narrator, consider whether he fulfilled the obligation of memorization, even if he used writing.
Writing aids but does not replace memorization.

وأما من جلس مجلس السماع، وهو يشتغل عنه بنظر في كتاب غير الذي يُقرأ، أو يَخُطُّ بقلم، أو يُعرِضُ عنه بلهو أو لعب، أو يغفل عنه بنوم أو كسل، فلا ضبط له ولا أمانة، ويُخاف عليه أن يُحرَم حَظِّه، والعياذ بالله، فلا تقوم الحجة بمثله ولا يتصل الإسناد بخبره، إلا ما يقع عن ضرورة : فإنه عفو، وصاحبه معذور.
* وإذا صح السماع وجب الحفظ إلى وقت الأداء، وذلك نوعان أيضاً تام، وما دونه عند المقابلة.
فالأول: عزيمة مطلقة، والثاني: رخصة انقلبت عزيمة.

As for the first: it is memorization without the medium of writing; this is a virtue that was specifically granted to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) because of the strength of the light of the heart, he was independent of writing. The Obligation of Preservation and Ruling on Writing Hadith
Discusses conditions for narrator reliability, obligation of preservation, and the dispute over writing hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding the obligation of hadith preservation and evaluate the evidence for permissibility of writing hadith.

Core Idea
Preservation of hadith is obligatory; writing hadith became sunna for preservation, reconciling early prohibitions.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses the trustworthiness of hadith narrators and the obligation to preserve hadith after valid hearing. It then delves into the historical debate over writing hadith, presenting evidence from the Companions both for and against, and concludes that writing became a sunna for preservation. Understanding this debate trains you in handling conflicting textual evidence (ta'arud al-adilla) and applying usul principles like naskh and tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of a reliable narrator
The passage begins by stating that a narrator who is negligent in reading, writing, or listening has no precision or trustworthiness. Identify what qualities are required for a narrator to be acceptable in hadith transmission.
This is a foundational condition for accepting reports (khabar).
2
Determine the ruling on preservation after valid hearing
The text says: 'If hearing is valid, preservation is obligatory until the time of performance.' Identify the type of obligation (wajib) and its basis in Hanafi usul.
Preservation is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) but emphasized individually.
3
Distinguish between the two types of preservation
The author says preservation is of two types: complete (azima) and incomplete (rukhsa turned into azima). Complete is without writing; incomplete is with writing. Understand how a concession becomes a firm obligation.
This distinction shows how rulings can evolve over time.
4
Analyze the dispute on writing hadith
The source presents arguments from companions who forbade writing and those who permitted. For each group, identify their key evidence: prohibitory hadith vs. permissive hadith and practice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf requiring usul tools to reconcile.
5
Apply the Hanafi reconciliation method
The author reconciles by noting that writing later became a sunna. Explain why the prohibitory evidence is considered abrogated or context-specific, and why the permissive evidence is stronger in Hanafi usul.
This trains you in tarjih (preference) and naskh (abrogation) principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي يُقرأ، أو يَخُطُّ بقلم، أو يُعرِضُ عنه بلهو أو لعب، أو يغفل عنه بنوم أو كسل، فلا ضبط له ولا أمانة، ويُخاف عليه أن يُحرَم حَظِّه، والعياذ بالله، فلا تقوم الحجة بمثله ولا يتصل الإسناد بخبره، إلا ما يقع عن ضرورة : فإنه عفو، وصاحبه معذور. وإذا صح السماع وجب الحفظ إلى وقت الأداء، وذلك نوعان أيضاً تام، وما دونه عند المقابلة. فالأول: عزيمة مطلقة، والثاني: رخصة انقلبت عزيمة. أما الأول : فالحفظ من غير واسطة الخط، وهذا فضل خُص به رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام؛ لقوة نور القلب، استغنى عن الخط، وكانوا لا يكتبون من قبل، ثم صارت الكتابةُ سُنَّةٌ في الكتاب والحديث؛ صيانةً. قوله : وكانوا لا يكتبون ليس كلهم، بل بعضهم. فممن كره ذلك: علي رضي الله عنه : روى عنه ابن أبي شيبة: «أعزِم على كل من كان عنده كتاب إلا رجع فمحاه، فإنما هلك الناس حيث تتبعوا أحاديث علمائهم، وتركوا كتاب ربهم». وأبو سعيد الخدري قد روى عنه ابن أبي شيبة : خذوا عنا كما أخذنا عن نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم. وابن مسعود : وأخرج عنه أنه كان يكره كتاب العلم. وروي عن الشعبي: «أن مروان دعا زيد بن ثابت وقوماً يكتبون وهو لا يدري، فأعلموه ، فقال : لعل كل حديث حدثتكم ليس كما حدثتكم». وعن سعيد بن جبير قال: كنا نختلف في أشياء، فكتبتها في كتاب، ثم أتيتُ بها ابن عمر أسأله عنها خفياً، فلو علم بها كانت الفيصل فيما بيني وبينه». وعن هارون بن عنترة عن أبيه عن ابن عباس : أنه رخص له أن يكتب ولم يكد. وحجة هذا ما رواه أبو داود عن المطلب بن عبد الله بن حنطب قال: «دخل زيد بن ثابت إلى معاوية فسأله معاوية عن حديث فحدثه، فأمر معاوية إنساناً يكتبه، فقال زيد : أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن لا نكتب شيئاً من حديثه، فمحاه». وما رواه مسلم عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا تكتبوا عني غير القرآن ومَن كتب غير القرآن : فليمحه». وممن أجاز ذلك عمر بن الخطاب فروى عنه ابن أبي شيبة أنه قال: «قيدوا العلم بالكتاب». وابن عباس : فروى عنه مثل لفظ عمر. والبراء، وأبو هريرة: روى ابن أبي شيبة عن عبد الله بن حنش قال: «رأيتهم عند البراء يكتبون على أكفهم بالقصب. وعن بشير بن نَهِيك قال: كنت أكتب ما أسمعه من أبي هريرة، فلما أردت أن أفارقه أتيتُه بكتابي فقلت: هذا سمعته منك، قال: نعم». وعن معن قال: «أخرج إلي عبد الرحمن بن عبد الله كتاباً، وحلف لي أنه خط أبيه بيده». وقد تقدم عنه أنه كره ذلك، والتوفيق فيه سهل. وحجة هذا ما روى أبو داود عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال : كنت أكتب كلّ شيء سمعته من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أريد حفظه فنهتني قريش قالوا: تكتب كل شيء ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بشر يتكلم في الرضا والغضب؟ فأمسكت عن الكتابة حتى ذكرت ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فأومأ بإصبعه إلى فيه، وقال: «اكتب، فوالذي نفسي بيده ما يخرج منه إلا حق». وما رواه الترمذي عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: شكى رجل من الأنصار فقال : يا رسول الله ! إني أسمع منك الحديث فيعجبني ولا أحفظه، فقال: «استعن بيمينك، وأومأ إلى الخط».
He who reads, or writes with a pen, or turns away from it with amusement or play, or neglects it due to sleep or laziness, has no precision and no trustworthiness, and it is feared that he will be deprived of his share, God forbid. So proof cannot be established through the likes of him, nor can the chain of transmission be connected through his report, except what occurs out of necessity: it is pardoned, and its owner is excused. And if hearing is valid, preservation is obligatory until the time of performance. That is also of two types: complete and that which is less upon comparison. The first is an absolute firm resolve, and the second is a concession that turned into a firm resolve. As for the first: it is preservation without the intermediary of writing. This is a virtue specifically given to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, due to the strength of the light of the heart, so he was independent of writing. And they used not to write before. Then writing became a sunnah in the Book and in hadith, for preservation. His statement: 'they used not to write' does not apply to all, but rather to some of them. Among those who disliked that: 'Ali, may God be pleased with him. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from him: 'I urge everyone who has a book with him to go back and erase it, for people only perished when they followed the hadiths of their scholars and abandoned the Book of their Lord.' And Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from him: 'Take from us as we took from our Prophet, peace be upon him.' And Ibn Mas'ud: It is narrated from him that he disliked writing knowledge. And it is narrated from al-Sha'bi: 'Marwan summoned Zayd ibn Thabit and some people who were writing without his knowledge, and they informed him. He said: Perhaps every hadith I narrated to you is not as I narrated it.' And from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: 'We used to differ on matters, so I wrote them down in a book, then I came to Ibn 'Umar asking him about them secretly. If he had known, it would have been the decisive factor between us.' And from Harun ibn 'Antara from his father from Ibn 'Abbas: that he permitted him to write and he did not refuse. The proof of this is what Abu Dawud narrated from al-Muttalib ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Hantab who said: 'Zayd ibn Thabit entered upon Mu'awiya, and Mu'awiya asked him about a hadith. He narrated it, and Mu'awiya ordered a person to write it down. Zayd said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, commanded us not to write anything of his hadith. So he erased it.' And what Muslim narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not write from me anything other than the Qur'an, and whoever wrote other than the Qur'an, let him erase it.' Among those who permitted it were 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: Ibn Abi Shayba narrated that he said: 'Tie down knowledge with writing.' And Ibn 'Abbas: he narrated similar wording from 'Umar. And al-Bara', and Abu Hurayra: Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from 'Abd Allah ibn Hanish who said: 'I saw them with al-Bara' writing on their palms with reed pens.' And from Bashir ibn Nahik who said: 'I used to write what I heard from Abu Hurayra. When I wanted to leave him, I brought my book to him and said: This I heard from you. He said: Yes.' And from Ma'n who said: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Abd Allah brought out a book to me and swore to me that it was the handwriting of his father.' And it has preceded from him that he disliked it, but reconciliation is easy. The proof of this is what Abu Dawud narrated from 'Abd Allah ibn 'Amr who said: I used to write everything I heard from the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, intending to memorize it. Quraysh forbade me, saying: You write everything while the Messenger of God is a human who speaks in pleasure and anger? So I stopped writing until I mentioned that to the Messenger of God. He pointed with his finger to his mouth and said: 'Write, for by the One in whose hand is my soul, nothing comes out of it except truth.' And what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Hurayra, may God be pleased with him, who said: A man from the Ansar complained: O Messenger of God, I hear from you a hadith that pleases me but I cannot memorize it. He said: 'Seek help with your right hand' and pointed to writing.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses the conditions of a trustworthy narrator and the preservation of hadith. The author first states that a narrator who is negligent—whether reading carelessly, writing absent-mindedly, or turning away in play—cannot be relied upon for proof or transmission, unless due to necessity. He then explains that once hearing (sama') is valid, preservation (hifz) until performance is obligatory. Preservation is of two types: complete (preservation without writing), which was a special virtue of the Prophet due to his pure heart, and a lesser form that requires comparison. Writing later became a sunna for preservation of both Qur'an and hadith. The author then presents the controversy: some companions disliked writing hadith, fearing it would lead to neglect of the Qur'an. He quotes 'Ali, Abu Sa'id, Ibn Mas'ud, and al-Sha'bi as examples. Evidence against writing includes hadith from Zayd ibn Thabit and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet forbade writing other than Qur'an. On the other hand, many companions permitted writing: 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, al-Bara', Abu Hurayra, and 'Abd Allah ibn 'Amr. The author then offers reconciliation by noting that the prohibition was early, before writing became necessary for preservation. The final proof is the hadith of 'Abd Allah ibn 'Amr where the Prophet explicitly permitted writing, and the hadith of Abu Hurayra where the Prophet told the man to 'seek help with his right hand' indicating writing. Thus, the relied-upon position is that writing hadith is permissible and even recommended for preservation.

Key Terms
الحفظ (al-hifz): Preservation of hadith in memory or writing until the time of narration
الكتابة (al-kitaba): Writing of hadith as a means of preservation
عزيمة (azima): A firm resolve or obligatory practice without concession
رخصة (rukhsa): A concession that may become a firm resolve under certain conditions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on writing hadith according to the Hanafi school as presented in this text?
A) It is absolutely forbidden
B) It is allowed only for the Prophet
C) It is permissible and recommended for preservation
D) It is a concession that is not preferred

Key Takeaway
Writing hadith is permissible and recommended for preservation, reconciling early prohibitions with later practice.

Written Records as Legal Proof: Mudhakkir vs Imam
Establishes Hanafi ruling on written notes as evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two categories of written records in Hanafi usul and apply the condition of 'reminder' (tadhkir) to determine whether a written note is a valid proof (hujjah).

Core Idea
Only writing that actually reminds the reader is a valid proof; a non-reminding record is void.

In the previous chapter on memorization (al-Dabt), we saw that reliable transmission requires retention. This chapter addresses writing as a tool for preservation. The Hanafi master al-Bazdawi presents a nuanced view: not all written records carry equal authority. By examining prophetic practice and logical analogy, we learn that the decisive factor is whether the writing serves as an effective reminder (mudhakkir) for the reader, regardless of the writer's identity. This lesson parses the key definitions and the dispute within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage and extract the two types of writing: mudhakkir (reminding) and imam (non-reminding). Note the author's statement that the first type is the original and has become an obligation.
The term 'imam' here is used in a unique sense meaning a record that does not remind, not a leader.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
List the hadith cited (Abu Shah, Abdullah ibn Amr, Rafi' ibn Khadij, Anas). Understand that they collectively establish the permissibility and commendability of writing down knowledge.
The hadith of Abu Shah includes the Prophet's explicit command to write.
3
Analyze the mirror analogy
Study Abu Hanifa's analogy: writing is to the heart like a mirror to the eye. If the mirror fails to convey an image, it is useless; similarly, if writing fails to produce remembrance, it is void (hader).
This analogy determines the hukm: only writing that actually reminds is a hujjah.
4
Distinguish the school positions
Note the reported disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds that non-reminding writing is absolutely invalid. Abu Yusuf (as reported by Bishr) holds that it is not to be acted upon in any of the three contexts (judge's register, hadith collections, documents). Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The passage does not give a tarjih; both are transmitted views.
5
Apply to a scenario
Take the example of a judge finding a written judgment he does not recall. According to Abu Hanifa, if the writing triggers his memory, it is valid; otherwise not. According to Abu Yusuf, it is never valid.
This practical case illustrates the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا: باب الكتابة والخط: وما رواه عنه أيضاً قال: خطب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر قصة في الحديث، فقال أبو شاه اكتبوا لي يا رسول الله، فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم: اكتبوا لأبي شاه. وما أخرج البخاري والترمذي عنه قال: ما كان في أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أكثر حديثاً عنه مني، إلا عبد الله بن عمرو، فإنه كان يكتب ولم أكتب. وما رواه الطبراني عن رافع بن خديج قال: قلت يا رسول الله! إنا نسمع منك أشياء فنكتبها قال اكتبوا ولا حرج. وعن أنس بن مالك قال: شكى رجل إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سوء الحفظ، فقال: استعن بيمينك. وعنه: أنه قال: قيدوا العلم بالكتاب.

وهذا يتصل بما سبق ذكره من باب الضبط، وهو نوعان: ١ - ما يكون مذكراً، وهو الأصل الذي انقلب عزيمة. وما يكون إماماً لا يفيد تذكرة. أما الذي يكون مذكراً: فهو حجة، سواء كان خطه، أو خط رجل معروف أو مجهول؛ لأن المقصود هو الذكر، والاحتراز عن النسيان غير ممكن، وإنما كان دوام الحفظ لرسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام، مع قوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَى إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ [الأعلى: 6-7]. وأما إذا كان الخط إماماً لا يذكره شيئاً فإن أبا حنيفة كان يقول: لا تحل الرواية بمثله بحال؛ لأن الخط للقلب بمنزلة المرآة للعين، والمرآة إذا تفد للعين دركاً كان عدماً، فالخط إذا لم يفد للقلب ذكراً كان هدراً. وإنما يدخل الخط في ثلاثة فصول: ١ - فيما يجده القاضي في ديوانه مما لا يذكره. ٢ - وما يكون في السنن والأحاديث. وما يكون في الصكوك. وروى بشر بن الوليد عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله: أنه لا يعمل به في ذلك كله. الله عن أبي حنيفة رحمه.
And this: the chapter on writing and script: And what was narrated from him (the Prophet) also: He addressed the people and mentioned a story in the hadith, so Abu Shah said: Write for me, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Write for Abu Shah. And what al-Bukhari and al-Tirmidhi narrated from him: There was no one among the Companions of the Messenger of Allah who had more hadith than me, except Abdullah ibn Amr, for he used to write and I did not write. And what al-Tabarani narrated from Rafi' ibn Khadij: I said: O Messenger of Allah! We hear things from you, so we write them down. He said: Write, and no harm. And from Anas ibn Malik: A man complained to the Messenger of Allah about poor memory, so he said: Seek help with your right hand. And from him: He said: Tie down knowledge with writing.

And this is connected to what was previously mentioned in the chapter on memorization (al-Dabt). It is of two types: 1. What is a reminder (mudhakkir) – this is the original that has become an obligation. And what is a leader (imam) that does not provide a reminder. As for that which is a reminder: it is a proof (hujjah), whether it is his own writing or the writing of a known or unknown person, because the objective is to remind, and avoiding forgetfulness is not possible. The permanence of memory was only for the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with His statement: We shall make you recite so you shall not forget except what Allah wills. But if the writing is a leader (imam) that does not remind him of anything, then Abu Hanifa used to say: It is not permissible to narrate by it under any circumstances, because writing is to the heart like a mirror to the eye. If the mirror fails to provide the eye with perception, it is nonexistent. So if writing does not provide the heart with remembrance, it is void. And writing falls into three categories: 1. What a judge finds in his register that he does not recall. 2. What is in the traditions (sunan) and hadith. And what is in documents (sikak). And Bishr ibn al-Walid narrated from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him: that it is not acted upon in all of that. Allah from Abu Hanifa, may He have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Bazdawi's Usul on the legal status of written records in transmitting knowledge and as evidence. The author begins by citing several hadith proving that writing was practiced and permitted by the Prophet. The hadith of Abu Shah shows the Prophet explicitly ordering writing for him. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr indicates he wrote while Abu Huraira did not, implying writing is not blameworthy. The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij shows general permission: 'Write, no harm.' The hadith of Anas recommends using the right hand for writing to aid memory. The author then states that this chapter connects to the previous one on memorization (al-Dabt). He divides writing into two types: (1) writing that serves as a reminder (mudhakkir) – this is the original method that has become a duty, and (2) writing that serves as a leader/record (imam) that does not provide a reminder. For the first type, it is a valid proof (hujjah) regardless of whether the writer is known or unknown, because the goal is to aid memory, and avoiding forgetfulness is impossible. He reinforces the exceptional status of the Prophet, who had permanent memory due to divine protection, citing the Quranic verse. For the second type, if the writing does not remind the reader of anything, Abu Hanifa rules it absolutely impermissible to rely on for narration. He gives an analogy: writing is to the heart as a mirror is to the eye; if the mirror fails to convey an image, it is useless. So if writing does not produce remembrance, it is worthless. Then he lists three contexts where such writing may be found: (1) a judge's own register that he does not recall, (2) texts of hadith and sunan, and (3) legal documents (sikak). Finally, he reports a narration from Bishr ibn al-Walid that Abu Yusuf held that it is not to be acted upon in all these cases. This indicates a difference within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa distinguishes between reminding and non-reminding writing, while Abu Yusuf appears to reject reliance on any written record that is not personally remembered. The text ends abruptly, possibly continuing with Abu Hanifa's full view.

Key Terms
الكتابة والخط (al-kitabah wa al-khatt): Writing and script, the act of inscribing or a written record
مذكر (mudhakkir): Writing that serves as a reminder, enabling the reader to recall content
إمام (imam): A written record that does not serve as a reminder; a leader/guide in the sense of being a source, but here it is the opposite
حجة (hujjah): Proof or evidence that is legally acceptable

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They must be written by a known and trustworthy person.
B) They must serve as a reminder to the reader (mudhakkir).
C) They must be from the Prophet's own dictation.
D) They must be certified by a judge.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a written record is only a valid proof if it actually functions as a reminder (mudhakkir) for the reader; otherwise, it is legally void.

The Two Modes of Hadith Transmission: Azima and Rukhsa
Introducing the two modes of transmission and the debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between azima (strict verbatim) and rukhsa (license to convey meaning) in hadith transmission, and explain the Hanafi position on conveying hadith by meaning.

Core Idea
Transmitting hadith verbatim is the ideal, but Hanafis permit conveying meaning when the transmitter is knowledgeable.

This lesson examines the two approaches to transmitting hadith texts: strict adherence to the exact wording ('azima) and the license to convey the meaning (rukhsa). We explore the proof cited by those who insist on verbatim transmission and the Hanafi response that allows flexibility. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating the reliability of hadith transmission in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Extract from the text the two terms: 'azima (determination) and rukhsa (license). Note that 'azima requires conveying the exact wording, while rukhsa permits conveying the meaning in the transmitter's own words.
The author immediately divides the 'aspect of transmission' into these two categories.
2
Understand the Evidence for Strict Verbatim
Some hadith scholars and language scholars argue that the hadith 'naddara Allahu imra'an sami'a minna maqalatan fa wa'aha wa addaha kama sami'aha' commands transmission as heard, implying verbatim is obligatory.
The hadith is cited with multiple chains, emphasizing its importance.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school holds that the hadith encourages careful transmission but does not prohibit conveying meaning when necessary, as long as the transmitter is knowledgeable and preserves the intended meaning.
The text itself presents the strict view but notes the existence of license, which the Hanafis adopt.
4
Recognize the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The dispute affects whether a hadith transmitted by meaning is considered reliable in fiqh. For Hanafis, it is valid if the transmitter was certain of the meaning; for strict literalists, only verbatim transmission is acceptable.
This difference impacts the classification of ahad hadith and their use as evidence.
5
Apply to a Hypothetical Scenario
Consider a narrator who heard a hadith but cannot recall the exact words, only the meaning. According to Hanafi usul, he may still transmit it if he is certain of the intended meaning. According to the strict view, he must not transmit it at all.
This illustrates the practical relevance of the two categories.

However, the author provides multiple variants of the hadith, indicating that the permissibility of conveying meaning is a debated issue. The Hanafi position generally allows conveying meaning if the transmitter is certain of the intended meaning, but here the text notes the strict view. This is important for understanding the transmission of hadith and the conditions for its acceptance.

Key Terms
عزيمة (azima): Strict adherence to the exact wording of the transmitted text
رخصة (rukhsa): License to convey the meaning of the transmitted text without sticking to the exact wording
تبليغ (tabligh): Transmission or conveyance of a text, especially hadith
نقل المتون (naql al-mutun): Transmission of the texts (matn) of hadith or other sacred writings

Key Takeaway

The Condition of Verbatim Transmission of Hadith Texts
Listing multiple hadith narrations to establish a usul rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul rule that transmitted hadith texts must be conveyed verbatim and identify the evidence from the hadith corpus.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command to convey his words 'as heard' establishes that any change in wording invalidates the hadith as legal proof.

In this chapter, Imam al-Bazdawi presents the foundational rule that prophetic hadiths must be transmitted exactly as heard, without paraphrasing. He supports this with multiple narrations of the famous hadith, all emphasizing the duty of accurate conveyance. This rule is crucial for Hanafi usul because the precise wording of a hadith can determine its legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The chapter title 'باب شرط نقل المتون' and the opening statement 'لا رخصة في هذا الباب' establish that the condition for transmitting texts is verbatim fidelity.
The author aligns with linguists and hadith scholars who forbid any license in this matter.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The core hadith: 'نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع منا مقالةً، فوعاها، وأداها كما سمعها' is presented as the main dalil.
Multiple chains from Ibn Mas'ud and others corroborate the same meaning.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'كما سمعها' (as he heard it) explicitly demands exact transmission. The verb 'أداها' implies delivery without alteration.
Other variants include 'فلم يزد فيه' (did not add to it), reinforcing the prohibition of alteration.
4
Consider variant narrations
The passage lists dozens of similar versions from various companions, all emphasizing comprehension (وعي) and verbatim conveyance.
The repetition underscores the importance and widespread transmission of this rule.
5
Understand the Hanafi application
In Hanafi usul, a hadith used as a legal proof must be transmitted verbatim. Paraphrasing is not permitted, as any change in wording could affect the ruling derived from it.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi methodology from some other schools that allow riwayah bi al-ma'na in certain contexts.

وفي لفظ : حديثاً : بدل : شيئاً.

وفي لفظ عند الدارمي: «نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع منا حديثاً فبلغه كما سمعه، فرب مبلغ أوعى من سامع». الحديث.
وعن عبيد بن عمير عن أبيه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطبهم فقال: «نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي ،فوعاها فرُبَّ حامل فقه لا فقهَ له، وربَّ حامل فقه إلى مَن هو أفقه منه».
وعن معاذ بن جبل قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نَضَرَ الله عبداً سمع كلامي فلم يزد فيه، فرب حامل فقه إلى أوعى منه». وفي لفظ : «نَضَرَ الله عبداً سمع مقالي فبلغه ، ثم لم يزد فيه، فرب حامل كلمة إلى من هو أوعى لها منه».
وعن النعمان بن بشیر أنه قال في خطبة: خطبنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مسجد الخيف، فقال: نضر الله وجهَ عبد سمع مقالتي فحملها، ربِّ حامل فقه غير فقيه، ورب حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه».
وعنه عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «رحم الله عبداً سمع مقالتي فحفظها، فرب حامل فقه غير فقيه، ورب حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه». وعن أبي قرصافة واسمه جَنْدَرةَ بن خَيْشَنة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي ،فوعاها وحفظها فربَّ حامل علم إلى مَن هو أعلم منه».
وعن جابر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نضر الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي : فوعاها، ثم بلغها، فرب مبلغ أوعى من سامع». وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نضر الله عبداً سمع مقالتي ،فوعاها فرب حامل فقه وهو غير فقيه ورب حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه».
Chapter on the condition of transmitting texts. Some of the people of hadith said: There is no license in this chapter, and I think it is the choice of the imams of language. They said: Because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a statement, comprehended it, and conveyed it as he heard it.' And (1) Chapter on the condition of transmitting texts: Hadith: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a statement, comprehended it, and conveyed it as he heard it.' I say: There are wordings with its meaning. Among them is what al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban, Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili, Ibn Abi Hatim in the Introduction to al-Jarh wa al-Ta'dil, Ibn Abi Khaythama, Abd al-Ghani ibn Sa'id in the book Adab al-Muhaddith, al-Khatib, and al-Uqayli narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us something and conveyed it as he heard it, for perhaps one who is conveyed to is more understanding than the one who heard.' In another wording: 'Hadith' instead of 'something'. In another wording: 'May Allah brighten a servant who heard my statement, memorized it, and conveyed it.' In another wording: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard my statement, comprehended it, and conveyed it.' And what al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ahmad, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and Ibn Abi Hatim in al-Muqaddima narrated from Zayd ibn Thabit: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a hadith and conveyed it.' In another wording: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a hadith, memorized it until he conveyed it to others.' The hadith. And what al-Tabarani narrated from Abu Darda: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ addressed us and said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard this statement of mine and conveyed it, for perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' The hadith. In another wording from al-Darimi: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a hadith and conveyed it as he heard it, for perhaps one who is conveyed to is more understanding than the one who heard.' The hadith. And from Ubayd ibn Umayr from his father that the Prophet ﷺ addressed them and said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard my statement and comprehended it, for perhaps a bearer of fiqh has no fiqh, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And from Muadh ibn Jabal: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a servant who heard my speech and did not add to it, for perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more understanding than him.' In another wording: 'May Allah brighten a servant who heard my statement and conveyed it, then did not add to it, for perhaps a bearer of a word may convey to one who is more understanding of it than him.' And from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir that he said in a sermon: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ addressed us in the Mosque of al-Khayf and said: 'May Allah brighten the face of a servant who heard my statement and carried it; perhaps a bearer of fiqh is not a faqih, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And from him from his father from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'May Allah have mercy on a servant who heard my statement and memorized it; perhaps a bearer of fiqh is not a faqih, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And from Abu Qarsafa, whose name is Jandara ibn Khayshana: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard my statement, comprehended it, and memorized it; perhaps a bearer of knowledge may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And from Jabir: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a person who heard my statement, comprehended it, then conveyed it; perhaps one who is conveyed to is more understanding than the one who heard.' And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah brighten a servant who heard my statement and comprehended it; perhaps a bearer of fiqh is not a faqih, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh may convey to one who is more knowledgeable than him.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the condition of transmitting texts (shart naql al-mutun) in a Hanafi usul work. The author begins by reporting that some hadith scholars and linguists hold that there is no license (rukhas) to convey prophetic sayings with paraphrasing; rather, one must transmit verbatim. They argue this on the basis of the well-known hadith, 'May Allah brighten a person who heard from us a statement, comprehended it, and conveyed it as he heard it.' The author then provides numerous variant narrations of this hadith from various companions, all emphasizing the duty to convey the Prophet's words exactly as heard, without addition or alteration. The core message is that the responsibility of transmitting sacred texts demands accuracy and fidelity. Imam al-Bazdawi, in his Kitab al-Uṣūl, includes this chapter to establish the methodological principle that the transmission of hadith must be with the exact wording, not merely the meaning. This principle is foundational for Hanafi usul, as it affects how evidence is derived from hadith. The passage is primarily a compilation of hadith evidence supporting this rule.

Key Terms
شرط نقل المتون (shart naql al-mutun): The condition that the text (matn) of a prophetic hadith must be transmitted verbatim, not paraphrased.
نَضَرَ الله امرءاً (naddara Allahu imra'an): A supplication meaning 'May Allah brighten/prosper a person', often interpreted as a prayer for freshness, honor, and happiness.
وعاها (wa'aha): Comprehended and memorized it thoroughly.
أداها كما سمعها (addaha kama sami'aha): Conveyed it exactly as he heard it, without addition, omission, or paraphrasing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadiths in this chapter, what is the primary condition for transmitting prophetic statements?
A) Convey the meaning, even if wording changes.
B) Convey the exact wording as heard, without addition or omission.
C) Convey only if the transmitter understands the fiqh implications.
D) Convey only if the listener is a scholar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul rule that transmitted hadith must be verbatim is firmly established by multiple hadith narrations commanding exact conveyance.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Accurate Transmission: Analyzing Multiple Narrations of 'نضر الله امرأ سمع مقالتي'
Compilation of hadiths urging accurate transmission of prophetic sayings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi usul principle derived from the multiple narrations of this hadith and apply it to evaluate whether a hadith may be narrated by meaning.

Core Idea
Prophetic comprehensive speech demands verbatim transmission; alteration is forbidden.

This passage collects numerous companion transmissions of a single prophetic supplication. At first glance, the text appears repetitive. Yet this very multiplicity is the point: it establishes the widespread (mutawatir) nature of the command to convey the Prophet's words exactly as heard. The commentary then links this to the Prophet's unique gift of 'jawami' al-kalim' (comprehensive speech), providing the usul rationale for why riwayah bil-lafz (verbatim narration) is obligatory in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core hadith and its variants
Read through the Arabic passage and note the common refrain 'نضر الله امرأ سمع مقالتي' across different companions. Observe the slight variations in wording—each emphasizes hearing, understanding, memorizing, and conveying without addition.
The author lists versions from Ubayd ibn Umayr, Muadh, al-Numan, Anas, Jabir, Sa'd, Jubayr, and Abu Sa'id.
2
Trace the repeated emphasis on accuracy
Pay attention to phrases like 'فبلغها كما سمعه', 'لم يزد فيه', 'ثم لم يزد فيه'. These consistently prohibit addition or alteration. The supplication 'نضر الله' is a prayer, but the context implies a strong recommendation (or even obligation) to preserve the exact wording.
The author explicitly states the Prophet's eloquence makes alteration unacceptable.
3
Recognize the rationale: jawami' al-kalim
After listing the narrations, the author adds 'ولأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مخصوص بجوامع الكلم' – because the Prophet was given comprehensive speech. This is the usul argument: the Prophet's words are concise yet packed with meaning; any change risks distorting the intended legal implication.
This is supported by the footnoted hadith from Abu Hurayrah and Abdullah ibn Amr.
4
Derive the usul principle: riwayah bil-lafz is required
From the combination of multiple chains (tawatur) and the unique nature of prophetic speech, Hanafi usul derives the rule that a hadith must be narrated verbatim. Narration by meaning (riwayah bil-ma'na) is only permitted when the wording is not considered part of the legal subject (e.g., in non-binding reports).
This differs from schools that allow riwayah bil-ma'na more freely, as seen in the Shafi'i position.
5
Apply the principle to evaluate narrator reliability
Using this principle, a narrator known to convey only the meaning (rather than exact words) may be deemed unreliable for transmitting legal hadiths. The multiple narrations here serve as evidence that the Prophet's companions understood the importance of exact wording.
This impacts the acceptance of khabar al-wahid: if a single narrator is careless with wording, his report may be rejected.

وعنه عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «رحم الله عبداً سمع مقالتي فحفظها، فرب حامل فقه غير فقيه، ورب حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه». وعن أبي قرصافة واسمه جَنْدَرةَ بن خَيْشَنة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي ،فوعاها وحفظها فربَّ حامل علم إلى مَن هو أعلم منه .
وعن جابر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نضر الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي فوعاها، ثم بلغها، فرب مبلغ أوعى من سامع». وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نضر الله عبداً سمع مقالتي ،فوعاها فرب حامل فقه وهو غير فقيه ورب حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه .
ولأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مخصوص بجوامع الكلم ، سابق في الفصاحة والبيان، فلا يُؤمَن في النقل التبديل والتحريف.
وعن أنس بن مالك قال: «خطبنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بمسجد الخيف من منى، فقال : نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي فحفظها ثم ذهب بها إلى من لم يسمعها ، فرُبَّ حامل فقه ليس بفقيه ، وربِّ حامل فقه إلى مَن هو أفقه منه». وفي لفظ : نَضَرَ الله مَن سمع قولي ، ثم لم يزد فيه». الحديث.
وأخرج هذا أيضاً الدارقطني في «الأفراد»، وأبو يعلى وابن أبي حاتم في «المقدمة».

And because he (peace be upon him) is specifically endowed with comprehensive speech, excelling in eloquence and clarity, so substitution and alteration are not safe in transmission. And from Anas ibn Malik said: 'The Messenger of Allah addressed us in the mosque of al-Khayf in Mina and said: May Allah brighten a person who hears my statement and memorizes it, then goes with it to one who has not heard it; for perhaps a bearer of fiqh is not a faqih, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh conveys it to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And in a wording: 'May Allah brighten one who hears my words, then does not add to it.' Hadith. And from Jubayr ibn Mutim said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say at al-Khayf, the Khayf of Mina: 'May Allah brighten a servant who hears my statement, memorizes it, understands it, and conveys it to one who has not heard it; a bearer of fiqh has no fiqh, and perhaps a bearer of fiqh conveys it to one who is more knowledgeable than him.' And this was also narrated by Ahmad, and it is in Ibn Majah with abbreviation. This is the end of what I know of its wordings, and it is evidence against the one who uses it as proof. And 'nādara' is with lightened dad, and Allah knows best. I say: it is predominant and it is permissible to double the dad, but lightening is better as in Maalim al-Sunan by al-Khattabi [5/253]. (1) His saying: 'And because he (peace be upon him) is specifically endowed with comprehensive speech': from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'I was sent with comprehensive speech.' Agreed upon. And from Abdullah ibn Amr said: 'The Messenger of Allah came out to us one day as if bidding farewell and said: I am the unlettered prophet, he said it three times, and there is no prophet after me; I have been given the opening words and comprehensive words.' Hadith narrated by Ahmad.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis: the author compiles multiple narrations of the hadith 'نضر الله امرأ سمع مقالتي' to demonstrate its wide transmission and to support the principle that prophetic statements must be conveyed accurately without addition or alteration. The author begins by quoting the core hadith with variations from Companions such as Ubayd ibn Umayr, Muadh ibn Jabal, al-Numan ibn Bashir, Anas ibn Malik, Jabir, Sad ibn Abi Waqqas, Jubayr ibn Mutim, and Abu Said al-Khudri. Each version emphasizes the virtue of hearing, understanding, memorizing, and faithfully transmitting the Prophet's words. The author then provides a rationale: the Prophet (peace be upon him) was given 'جوامع الكلم' (comprehensive speech) and surpassed all in eloquence, so any alteration in transmission is unacceptable. This is reinforced by a footnote citing two hadiths: one from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet was sent with 'جوامع الكلم', and another from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Prophet was given 'فواتح الكلم وجوامعه'. The author concludes that this collection of narrations serves as evidence against those who might claim the hadith is weak or isolated. The linguistic note on 'نضر' (pronounced with lightened or doubled dad) shows attention to precise recitation. In Hanafi usul, this passage is used to establish the obligation of accurate narration (riwayah bil-lafz) and the prohibition of narrating by meaning (riwayah bil-ma'na) for prophetic hadiths, especially when dealing with texts that are mu'jiz (miraculous in eloquence). This principle impacts the acceptance of khabar al-wahid and the conditions for its validity.

Key Terms
جوامع الكلم (jawami' al-kalim): Comprehensive speech; words that are concise yet encompass many meanings, a gift given to the Prophet.
نضر (nādara / naḍḍara): A verb meaning 'may Allah brighten' or 'grant radiance', used as a supplication; its correct pronunciation is with lightened dad (nādara) but allowed with shaddah.
رِوَايَةٌ باللَّفْظِ (riwayah bil-lafz): Narrating a hadith by repeating the exact words of the Prophet, as opposed to conveying the meaning (riwayah bil-ma'na).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the author includes so many different narrations of the same hadith?
A) To show that the hadith has multiple chains, making it mutawatir and thus a stronger proof.
B) To demonstrate that the Companions disagreed on the wording.
C) To prove that the Prophet spoke the exact same words on many occasions.
D) To argue that the supplication 'نضر الله' is the main point, not the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
The multiple narrations of the hadith 'نضر الله امرأ سمع مقالتي' establish the obligation to transmit prophetic words verbatim, grounded in the Prophet's unique gift of comprehensive speech.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Permissibility of Riwaya bi al-Ma'na: Hanafi Usul Principle
Ruling on riwaya bi al-ma'na with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position on riwaya bi al-ma'na and identify the key evidence from hadith and consensus.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul permits conveying hadith by meaning because the wording of Sunnah is not miraculous; its purpose is the meaning.

This lesson addresses a fundamental usul al-fiqh issue: can a hadith be narrated by its meaning rather than its exact wording? The Hanafi school, following the practice of the Companions and the majority of scholars, permits this as a concession (rukhsa). We will examine the primary evidence from the Prophet's own encouragements and the reasoning behind the permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Begin by noting that the passage asserts the permissibility (لا بأس) of conveying hadith by meaning in general, but as a concession (رخصة). Understand that 'meaning' here refers to the intended legal message, not the exact wording.
The concession applies to hadith, not to the Quran.
2
Examine the key hadith evidence
Read the hadith 'نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي فحفظها ثم ذهب بها إلى من لم يسمعها' and variants. Focus on the phrase 'لم يزد فيه' (does not add to it). This indicates that adding is prohibited, but omitting or paraphrasing is not forbidden.
The hadith is used as proof that conveying the meaning is sufficient, as long as nothing is added.
3
Analyze the Companions' practice as consensus
The author cites that the Companions would say 'أمرنا رسول الله بكذا' or 'قال رسول الله كذا أو نحواً منه' (or similar to it). This shows they did not require verbatim transmission, providing a practical consensus.
This consensus (ijma) is a strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the opposing view and the Hanafi response
Some scholars argued for verbatim transmission because the Prophet was given 'jawami' al-kalim' (comprehensive speech) and was foremost in eloquence. The Hanafi response: the wording of Sunnah is not miraculous like the Quran; its purpose is the meaning, and the Companions themselves paraphrased.
The text explicitly states 'النظم من السنة غير معجز' (the wording of Sunnah is not miraculous).
5
Derive the usul principle
From this passage, the Hanafi principle is: Narrating hadith by meaning is permissible provided the meaning is accurately preserved and no addition distorts it. This principle is relied upon in legal reasoning (istinbat).
This is a key distinction from the Quran, where even the wording is considered miraculous (i'jaz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مخصوص بجوامع الكلم ، سابق في الفصاحة والبيان، فلا يُؤمَن في النقل التبديل والتحريف. وعن أنس بن مالك قال: «خطبنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بمسجد الخيف من منى، فقال : نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي فحفظها ثم ذهب بها إلى من لم يسمعها ، فرُبَّ حامل فقه ليس بفقيه ، وربِّ حامل فقه إلى مَن هو أفقه منه». وفي لفظ : «نَضَرَ الله مَن سمع قولي ، ثم لم يزد فيه». الحديث. وأخرج هذا أيضاً الدارقطني في «الأفراد»، وأبو يعلى وابن أبي حاتم في «المقدمة». وعن جبير بن مطعم قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول بالخيف خيف مني: «نَضَرَ الله عبداً سمع مقالتي فحفظها ووعاها، وبلغها من لم يسمعها، حامل فقه لا فقهَ له، وربَّ حامل فقه إلى من هو أفقه منه». وفي لفظ : «نَضَرَ الله وجهَ امرئ سمع مقالتي فوعاها حتى يبلغها من لم يسمعها»، وهذا رواه أحمد أيضاً ، وهو في ابن ماجه باختصار. وما روى البزار عن أبي سعيد الخدري عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال في حجة الوداع: «نَضَرَ الله امرءاً سمع مقالتي فوعاها فرب حامل فقه ليس بفقيه». انتهى ما علمتُ من ألفاظه، وهو حجة على المحتج به. ونَضَرَ بتخفيف الضاد، والله أعلم. قلت ويجوز بتشديد الضاد، لكن التخفيف أجود كما في معالم السنن للخطابي. قوله : ولأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مخصوص بجوامع الكلم : عن أبي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : «بعثت بجوامع الكلم». متفق عليه. وعن عبد الله بن عمرو قال: «خرج علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوماً كالمودع فقال: أنا النبي الأمي ، قالها ثلاث مرات، ولا نبي بعدي، أُوتيتُ فواتح الكلم، وجوامعه». الحديث رواه أحمد. وقال عامة العلماء: لا بأس بذلك في الجملة رخصة؛ لاتفاق الصحابة على قولهم : أَمَرَنا رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بكذا، ونهانا عن كذا. وعن ابن مسعود وغيره: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا ، أو نحواً منه، أو قريباً منه. وفي تفصيل الرخصة جواب عما قال، وهذا لأن النظم من السنة غير معجز، وإنما النظم لمعناه، بخلاف القرآن.
And because he (peace be upon him) is distinguished by comprehensive speech, foremost in eloquence and clarity, so one cannot be safe from substitution and distortion in transmission. And from Anas ibn Malik: 'The Messenger of Allah addressed us in the mosque of al-Khayf in Mina, saying: May Allah brighten (the face of) a person who hears my speech and memorizes it, then conveys it to those who have not heard it, for perhaps a carrier of fiqh is not a faqih, and perhaps a carrier of fiqh carries it to one who is more learned than him.' And in another wording: 'May Allah brighten (the face of) the one who hears my speech and then does not add to it.' The hadith. And this was also narrated by al-Daraqutni in al-Afrad, and Abu Ya'la and Ibn Abi Hatim in al-Muqaddimah. And from Jubayr ibn Mut'im: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say at al-Khayf, the Khayf of Mina: May Allah brighten a servant who hears my speech, memorizes it, retains it, and conveys it to those who have not heard it; a carrier of fiqh who has no fiqh, and perhaps a carrier of fiqh carries it to one who is more learned than him.' And in another wording: 'May Allah brighten the face of a person who hears my speech and retains it until he conveys it to those who have not heard it.' This is also narrated by Ahmad, and in Ibn Majah it is summarized. And what al-Bazzar narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri from the Prophet that he said during the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'May Allah brighten a person who hears my speech and retains it, for perhaps a carrier of fiqh is not a faqih.' End of what I know of its wordings, and it is an argument against the one who uses it as evidence. And 'nadhara' with lightening of the dad, and Allah knows best. I say: and it is permissible with tashdid, but lightening is better as in Ma'alim al-Sunan by al-Khattabi. His statement: 'And because he is distinguished by comprehensive speech': from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'I was sent with comprehensive speech.' Agreed upon. And from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'The Messenger of Allah came out to us one day as if bidding farewell and said: I am the unlettered prophet, three times, and no prophet after me; I have been given the openings of speech and its comprehensive forms.' The hadith narrated by Ahmad. And the majority of scholars said: there is no harm in that (conveying by meaning) generally as a concession; due to the consensus of the Companions on their statement: 'The Messenger of Allah commanded us such-and-such, forbade us such-and-such.' And from Ibn Mas'ud and others: 'The Messenger of Allah said such-and-such, or similar to it, or close to it.' And in the details of the concession is a response to what was said, and this is because the wording of the Sunnah is not miraculous; rather, the wording is for its meaning, unlike the Quran.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning (riwaya bi al-ma'na) rather than verbatim. The author begins by noting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was given 'jawami' al-kalim' (comprehensive speech) and was superior in eloquence, which might suggest a need for exact transmission. However, he then presents multiple hadiths where the Prophet himself encourages conveying his speech even if the wording is not preserved exactly, such as the well-known hadith 'May Allah brighten a person who hears my speech...' The wording 'and does not add to it' indicates that adding is prohibited, but omitting or paraphrasing is not forbidden. The author then cites the practice of the Companions, who would say 'the Messenger of Allah said such-and-such or similar to it, or close to it,' showing their use of approximate wording. The majority of scholars (aimmah) ruled that this is permissible as a concession (rukhas), based on the consensus of the Companions. The reasoning is that the wording of the Sunnah is not miraculous ('غير معجز') like the Quran; its meaning is what matters. Therefore, conveying the meaning is acceptable as long as the meaning is accurately preserved. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul: the permissibility of riwaya bi al-ma'na for hadith, unlike the Quran where exact wording is required.

Key Terms
جوامع الكلم (jawami' al-kalim): Comprehensive speech that conveys many meanings in few words, a special gift to the Prophet.
رخصة (rukhsa): A concession or dispensation, allowing something that might otherwise be prohibited.
riwaya bi al-ma'na (riwaya bi al-ma'na): Narrating a hadith by its meaning rather than its exact wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Companions say 'أو نحواً منه أو قريباً منه' when narrating hadith?
A) They forgot the exact wording.
B) To indicate permissibility of conveying meaning rather than verbatim.
C) To show doubt in their memory.
D) To distinguish between Quran and hadith.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul permits conveying hadith by meaning, relying on the Prophet's own words and the Companions' consensus, based on the principle that the wording of Sunnah is not miraculous.

Five Categories of Reports (Khabar) According to Certainty
Classification of khabar by certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the five categories of khabar based on their level of certainty and recall their definitions.

Core Idea
Reports vary in certainty: mutawatir (certain), mashhur (probable with doubt), ahad (preponderant), suspended, and rejected.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all reports carry the same weight. The scholars classified narrations (khabar) according to the degree of certainty they provide. This classification is essential for determining which reports can serve as binding proof (hujja) in deriving rulings. This lesson walks you through the five categories defined by Imam al-Bazdawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories
List the five divisions in order: (1) mutawatir, (2) mashhur, (3) ahad, (4) suspended (mawquf), (5) impugned (mat'un).
Memorise this sequence; it reflects decreasing certainty.
2
Understand the criterion
Each category is defined by its level of doubt (shubha) and the presence or absence of countervailing evidence.
Mutawatir has no doubt; mashhur has some doubt; ahad is probable; suspended loses preponderance due to a counter-proof; impugned is rejected.
3
Analyse the fifth category sub-types
The impugned report splits into two: rejection due to the narrator himself (e.g., lying, weak memory) or due to external reasons (e.g., contradiction with a stronger source).
This distinction helps identify the proper remedy (jarh wa ta'dil).
4
Connect to fiqh application
Only mutawatir and sound ahad (under conditions) can establish rulings. Mashhur gives probabilistic knowledge, while suspended and impugned are not binding.
This classification directly impacts which hadith are used in istidlal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب تقسيم الخبر من طريق المعنى وهو خمسة أقسام : 1- ما هو صدق لا شبهة فيه، وهو خبر الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام، وذلك هو المتواتر منه. 2- وقسم فيه شبهة، وهو المشهور. 3- وقسم محتمل ترجح جانب صدقه، وهو ما مر من أخبار الآحاد. 4- وقسم محتمل، عارض دليل رجحان الصدق منه ما أوجب وقفه، فلم تقم به الحجة، وذلك مثل ما سبق من أنواع ما يسقط به خبر الواحد. 5- والقسم الخامس : الخبر المطعون الذي ردَّه السلفُ، وأنكروه. وهذا القسم نوعان: نوع: لحقه الطعن والنكير من راوي الحديث. ونوع آخر : ما لحقه ذلك من جهة غير الراوي. وهذا باب ما يلحقه النكير من قبل راويه :
Chapter: Division of the report from the perspective of meaning. It is five divisions: 1) That which is true without any doubt, and it is the report of the Messenger (peace be upon him), and that is the mutawatir among them. 2) A division with some doubt, and it is the mashhur. 3) A division that is probable with the side of its truth preponderating, and it is what has passed regarding ahad reports. 4) A division that is probable, but a preponderance of truth has been opposed by a proof that necessitates its stoppage, so it does not establish proof, and that is like the types mentioned previously by which a single-narrator report is dropped. 5) The fifth division: the report that is impugned, which the predecessors rejected and disapproved. This division is of two types: a type that suffers impugnment and rejection from the narrator of the hadith, and another type that suffers that from a source other than the narrator. This is the chapter of what attaches rejection from the side of its narrator.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a classification of reports (khabar) based on their level of certainty. The author divides them into five categories. The first is the report that is absolutely true with no doubt: the mutawatir report of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The second is the mashhur report, which has some doubt but is widely transmitted. The third is the ahad report, where the side of truth is preponderant but it remains probable. The fourth is a report that is probable but a countervailing proof suspends it, so it does not constitute a binding proof—these are cases like a single-narrator report that has been dropped due to some defect. The fifth category is the impugned report rejected by the early scholars. This itself splits into two: rejection due to the narrator himself, and rejection due to an external reason. The passage concludes by announcing a chapter on rejection arising from the narrator.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration; in usul al-fiqh, it refers to a statement conveying information about the past, often a hadith.
متواتر (mutawātir): A report transmitted by so many narrators at each level that it is impossible for them to have conspired on a lie, yielding certain knowledge.
مشهور (mashhūr): A report that is widely transmitted but not to the level of tawatur; it is below mutawatir but above solitary, and carries some doubt.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur or mashhur; it is probable but not certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which category of report is considered true without any doubt?
A) The mashhur report
B) The mutawatir report
C) The ahad report
D) The impugned report

Key Takeaway
The classification of khabar into five levels of certainty is foundational for evaluating the probative value of hadith in Hanafi usul.

Four Grounds for Rejection of a Report from the Narrator's Side
Listing four grounds for rejecting a report from the narrator's side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four grounds for rejecting a report from the narrator's side and explain the Hanafi approach to each.

Core Idea
A report can be rejected if the narrator denies, acts inconsistently, restricts meaning, or refrains from acting.

In this passage, al-Pazdawi enumerates four ways a narrator can disqualify his own report. Understanding these grounds is essential for evaluating hadith reliability in Hanafi usul. This lesson walks through each category and its implications for legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the four categories
The passage begins by stating there are four divisions (أربعة أقسام) of rejection from the narrator's side. Identify each one as listed: (1) explicit denial, (2) acting contrary before/after/dating unknown, (3) specifying interpretation or specification, (4) refraining from action.
These are internal flaws (qadih) in the narrator that weaken the report's reliability.
2
Analyze the first ground: denial
The narrator explicitly denies having narrated the report. This is the most severe and triggers a dispute among scholars, which will be covered in the next lesson.
Denial can be explicit (صريح) or implied; here it is explicit.
3
Analyze the second ground: inconsistent action
The narrator acts contrary to the report before it reached him (showing he was unaware), after it reached him (implying rejection), or the date is unknown (making it uncertain which came first).
If the date is known and the contrary action preceded the report, it may indicate abrogation (naskh) or forgetfulness.
4
Analyze the third ground: specifying interpretation
The narrator himself interprets the report in a specific way or applies a specification (takhsis), thereby restricting its general meaning. This does not reject the report but limits its scope.
This is not a full rejection but a qualification (ta'yin) of one possible meaning.
5
Analyze the fourth ground: refraining from action
The narrator refrains from acting upon the report, which may indicate he does not consider it binding or has some doubt.
Refraining (imtina') is weaker than denial but still raises questions about the report's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يلحقه النكير من قبل الراوي ولهذا النوع أربعة أقسام : 1- ما أنكره صريحاً. 2- والثاني : أن يعمل بخلافه قبل أن يبلغه، أو بعد ما بلغه، أو لا يُعرف تاريخه. 3- والقسم الثالث: أن يُعين بعض ما احتمله الحديث من تأويل أو تخصيص. 4- والرابع: أن يمتنع عن العمل به. أما إذا أنكر المروي عنه الرواية، فقد اختلف فيه السلف : فقال بعضهم: لا يسقط العمل به. وقال بعضهم : يسقط العمل به، وهذا أشبه. وقد قيل : إن قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله : أن يسقط الاحتجاج به، وقال محمد رحمه الله : لا يسقط. وهو فرع اختلافهما في شاهدين شهدا على القاضي بقضية، وهو لا يذكرها : فقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : لا تُقبل، وقال محمد رحمه الله : تُقبل.
Chapter: What attaches rejection from the side of the narrator. This type has four divisions: 1) That which he explicitly denies. 2) The second: that he acts contrary to it before it reaches him, or after it reaches him, or the date is unknown. 3) The third division: that he specifies some interpretation or specification that the hadith possibly allows. 4) The fourth: that he refrains from acting upon it. As for when the one narrated from denies the narration, the predecessors differed about it. Some said: it does not drop acting upon it. And some said: it drops acting upon it, and this is more appropriate. It has been said that the opinion of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) is that it drops the argument, and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it does not drop. And it is a branch of their disagreement in the case of two witnesses who testified before a judge about a case that he does not remember. Abu Yusuf said: they are not accepted, and Muhammad said: they are accepted.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage discusses the grounds for rejecting a report due to the narrator. It lists four types: (1) the narrator explicitly denies the report; (2) the narrator acts contrary to the report before it reaches him, or after it reaches him, or the date of his action is unknown; (3) the narrator specifies an interpretation or specification that the hadith might allow, thereby restricting its meaning; (4) the narrator refrains from acting upon the report entirely. The text then focuses on the first type—when the person from whom the report is narrated (the narrator himself) denies having narrated it. The early scholars differed: some said the report is not dropped (i.e., still acceptable), while others said it is dropped. The author states that the latter view (dropping) is more appropriate (أشبه). He then reports a more specific position: Abu Yusuf held that it drops the argument (i.e., the report is no longer valid proof), while Muhammad al-Shaybani held that it does not drop. This disagreement is traced to a fundamental difference in a case: two witnesses testify before a judge about a case that the judge does not remember. Abu Yusuf says their testimony is not accepted (because the judge’s non-remembrance implies denial), while Muhammad says it is accepted. So the ruling on the narrator’s denial follows the same principle.

Key Terms
إنكار (inkār): Denial; here refers to the narrator's explicit denial of having narrated a report.
المروي عنه (al-marwī ʿanhu): The person from whom the report is narrated—i.e., the narrator himself.
السلف (as-salaf): The early generations of Muslims, particularly the Companions and Successors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four grounds for rejection from the narrator's side?
A) Explicit denial
B) Acting contrary before or after the report
C) Narrator's weak memory
D) Refraining from acting upon the report

Key Takeaway
A report can be rejected when the narrator explicitly denies it, acts inconsistently, qualifies its meaning, or refrains from acting upon it.

The Narrator's Denial: Dispute Between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Dispute over the effect of narrator's denial, linked to a witness testimony analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a narrator's denial and apply the underlying analogy from witness testimony.

Core Idea
If a narrator denies having narrated a report, Abu Yusuf drops the report; Muhammad retains it, analogizing to witnesses testifying before a forgetful judge.

The first ground for rejection—explicit denial—was the subject of debate among early scholars. This lesson explores the internal Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, tracing it back to a foundational difference in accepting witness testimony before a judge who does not remember. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate narrator reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The passage reports that when the narrator denies the report, some said the report is dropped, others said it is not dropped. The author says the dropping view is 'more appropriate' (أشبه). Then it specifies Abu Yusuf's view: the report drops as argument; Muhammad's: it does not drop.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school; both are from the madhhab.
2
Understand the branch case
The difference is a branch (فرع) of their disagreement about two witnesses testifying before a judge about a case he does not remember. Abu Yusuf says the testimony is not accepted (because the judge's non-remembrance is like denial). Muhammad says it is accepted (because the judge may have forgotten, just as the narrator may have forgotten).
This analogy reveals the underlying principle: does denial necessarily imply falsity, or could it be due to forgetfulness?
3
Apply to the narrator's denial
Using the same reasoning, Abu Yusuf says the narrator's denial means the report is false, so it is dropped. Muhammad says the narrator may have forgotten, so the report remains valid proof.
The disagreement is not about the report's authenticity but about the legal effect of the narrator's denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يلحقه النكير من قبل الراوي ولهذا النوع أربعة أقسام : 1- ما أنكره صريحاً. 2- والثاني : أن يعمل بخلافه قبل أن يبلغه، أو بعد ما بلغه، أو لا يُعرف تاريخه. 3- والقسم الثالث: أن يُعين بعض ما احتمله الحديث من تأويل أو تخصيص. 4- والرابع: أن يمتنع عن العمل به. أما إذا أنكر المروي عنه الرواية، فقد اختلف فيه السلف : فقال بعضهم: لا يسقط العمل به. وقال بعضهم : يسقط العمل به، وهذا أشبه. وقد قيل : إن قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله : أن يسقط الاحتجاج به، وقال محمد رحمه الله : لا يسقط. وهو فرع اختلافهما في شاهدين شهدا على القاضي بقضية، وهو لا يذكرها : فقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : لا تُقبل، وقال محمد رحمه الله : تُقبل.

This type has four divisions: 1) That which he explicitly denies. 2) The second: that he acts contrary to it before it reaches him, or after it reaches him, or the date is unknown. 3) The third division: that he specifies some interpretation or specification that the hadith possibly allows. 4) The fourth: that he refrains from acting upon it. إنكار (inkār): Denial; here refers to the narrator's explicit denial of having narrated a report.
المروي عنه (al-marwī ʿanhu): The person from whom the report is narrated—i.e., the narrator himself.
السلف (as-salaf): The early generations of Muslims, particularly the Companions and Successors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Muhammad's view that a narrator's denial does not drop the report?
A) The narrator's denial is always false
B) The judge's forgetfulness analogy shows denial may be due to forgetfulness
C) The report is mutawatir
D) The narrator is a Companion

Key Takeaway
When a narrator denies a report, Abu Yusuf drops it as proof, while Muhammad retains it based on the analogy of witnesses before a forgetful judge.
